<Text>I was so excited to eat at Oenotri as they are recommended in Michelin guide and claim to offer Neapolitan pizza from the traditional stone oven. I‚Äôve been to Naples, Italy and LOVE Neapolitan pizza. While the place was nice and full of people, the two pizzas that we ordered - classic margarita and zucchini - were not even close to the pizza I ate in Naples. < review>
We had only one dinner in Napa on a short trip, so I was obsessing over where to go. We ultimately chose Oenotri because of its location close to our hotel, the unique and constantly-changing items on the menu, the more laid-back vibe, and of course, the food that gets consistently rave reviews. We chose well!

Our server was Devany, and we adored her immediately. We ordered a cocktail each, feeling a bit wined out from our first-ever tasting day in Napa, then decided on sharing the Intenso pizza and a pasta ragu with meat sauce and fusilli noodles. As a couple who generally avoids carbs, we were over the moon in love with our indulgent meal! The Intenso is a very non-traditional pizza that includes pistachios and red onions, no red sauce to be found. The pasta was literal perfection, reminded us of a rustic Old World-style pasta dish, and we about got into a fight over licking the bowl clean.

For dessert, we chose the panna cotta and it was delightful. We learned that Oenotri grows and uses many of its ingredients, including herbs, berries, and Meyer lemons, and you could taste the freshness in everything.

The service is team-style, which we really appreciated. We always had full glasses and never had any dirty plates or anything, plus everyone is extremely knowledgeable and friendly. The ambiance is romantic and cozy, but very laid-back. Prices are also super reasonable, a pleasant surprise in this area. Knowing how many incredible restaurant choices there are in Napa, we would happily come back here!< /review>

0x8085065d44d04ad3:0x5c8a199dd2540770<//gmapID>
<resp>None< /resp>< Review>
Stellar.  Delicious.  Very well-crafted food from fresh ingredients, and the first place in North America that my partner has loved the pasta alla carbonara!  My gigli pasta in a pork ragout was comfort food raised to an art form.  The pizza we shared for a starter was perfectly done.  Their menu selection of pizzas was a bit odd, only one appealed to us but that one turned out to be excellent.  Their menu changes daily so take my kvetching about that selection with a grain of salt, and I'm guessing they'll probably make you a custom pizza (within reason) if you ask, because it's a high-service sort of place.

Don't just look at the dessert menu if you like a drink after dinner... they have a nice assortment of excellent grappa and I'm sure many other things besides the selections mentioned on the dessert card.

It's a bit of a noisy place, with hard surfaces and a bunch of people chatting (likely about how much they were enjoying dinner) so keep that in mind if you need a quiet dinner experience, but if you want excellent food in the Italian tradition of fresh, high-quality ingredients and careful prep.  We'll be back.</Review>

< text>
Came in on a Friday night for dinner around 21:00hrs and got a table for two right away. Picked out a bottle of Chenin Blanc and our waiter Damian was able to help us choose some complimenting dishes. We had the yellowfin crudo, Torchio with short rib, and Tagliatelle with shrimp.  Tuna was nice and simple and fresh, pasta for both dishes were nice and firm and had good flavor. One beefy, but not overly powering, and the shrimp had a good seafood taste, but may be too fishy for some, like my dining companion.

We had the chocolate cannoncini for dessert, described as a  croissant with chocolate cream. Was a bit harder than I expected, but soft tasting finish to the meal.  Would have preferred a darker chocolate taste.

Would return again if I was in the area.

Damian was knowledgeable about their food and made great recommendations to cater to our tarred and was pleasant throughout the whole dinner.<//text>

< Review>
We visited our first night in Napa since Oenotri was one of the few places open past 8pm.  The iPad wine list was fairly extensive and featured a number of excellent, affordable Italian wines in addition to the overpriced California ones.  Needless to say, we chose a Montefalco that complemented our meat perfectly. The salumi were all terrific, the salads fresh and the meats tender. < user_name>

<date>1401817900046< /date>< text>
I was in Napa on vacation and asked Adam at the Vitners collective where he'd recommend for the best neapolitan Pizza in the area, without hesitation he effused about Oenotri.  So we tried it for dinner , and it wasn't as advertised it was transcendent!  I obsess over neapolitan Pizza, everywhere I go and including New York and my hometown of Cleveland, this is the new number one for me.  It was so good, my wife and I returned the next day for lunch and waited a half hour to be among the first to eat.  Also, tried the trompotti pasta, which was akin to eating candy, light perfectly paired with a simple cream based sauce with fresh split peas,green garlic and pesto.  The freshness of all the produce we had is hard to fairly describe, it's almost a secret weapon here.  But the dough deserves it, they even lavish a pre coat of 1 month old or less olive oil , then a second coat after baking.  between the overnite rise and the attention to detail the result is a crust that is the perfect balance of lightness and pliable crispness.  Bravo!< /text>

<resp>None< /resp><Pics>None< /Pics><GmapID>0x80c2b0cd5f663c1f:0x21f0b6203a68cea8<//GmapID><rating>5< /rating></record>

<Resp>None</Resp>< review>
Ive been coming here over the years since Ive worked at LAX. Sometimes its hard to make time to find a good deli/sub shop that can make good food within a matter of minutes to get back to work so Im used to the quiznos/subway lifestyle. But I found this gem randomly when I first started using YELP and still to this day I would recommend this to anyone whos looking for authentic deli food and sandwiches. Located in westchester in the la tijera triangle plaza,owned and operated by family, they provide delicious sides and sandwiches from the #3 Ham, capicolla and proscuitto which has always been and always will be my favorite..because how can you go wrong with any sub that puts prosciutto in it?!

Now, dont get me wrong..I love this place so much but Ive noticed that yes, they have lessened the amount of meat they put on the sandwiches because my meal last week, even the 14" didnt really seem filling and I had more veggies than the meat itself. Also, since they have done more catering, which is great for them, unfortunately being only open from 11:30-5 is kind of a letdown because I think they could make just as much money if not more if they were open a little earlier because so many people at my job who have had it now would love to get an early breakfast or lunch from them. But thats the thing of small businesses and how they chose to operate.< /review>

LA Fitness, Los Angeles, California

I was a member of Bally's for many, many years, however, one day they shut down and LA Fitness took them over and has done such a Fantastic Job Ever Since!

I am a Proud Member of LA Fitness where You Can Develop Your Body Into Being The Best That You Can Be!

Their gyms have many things to do such as aerobic classes, weight training, zumba classes, yoga classes, swimming pools, boot camp classes, body conditioning classes, etc.

You can Never get bored at LA Fitness!

I just started going back because I need to Lose Weight and I have been going every day taking their Zumba and Yoga Classes and I am more than sure that My Body Will Be Changing Very Soon For The Better!

I really enjoy coming to LA Fitness and they definitely have programs to suit All Of Your Body's Needs!

In the following pictures, I was taking a Zumba Class with Gloria Jimenez who is one of their Top Instructors.

< Review>
I can't say that any of the LA fitnesses I have visited have been okay. This one on Wilshire in LA is decent but the lady leading the Tuesday night class was horrible. I felt like it was such a waste of time. She didn't know how to teach, she didn't count down properly, she had the music way too fast and we were slinging weights all over the place to the point that it was unsafe. I finally stopped doing what she was doing and did my own thing during the class. I'm not sure why they keep her as an instructor.

The gym is small, which is fine and it seems that most of the equipment is okay compared to other LA Fitness is where most of the equipment is broken. However there are not nearly enough mats for Pilates, yoga and other classes. If you want a mat you have to go around the gym to see if you can find one and there's probably less than 20 in the whole gym.

I spoke with a member who has been attending that gym for several years because she lives nearby. She says they always struggle to keep good instructors. I only tried it out because it's closer to my house but I like the instructors at the La Cienega LA Fitness much better. If this LA Fitness obtain some good instructors I would definitely want to return.</Review>

Weight and workout facilities only....par for the course.   As a "gym" it's very awkwardly laid out, with locker rooms in adjacent building, and VERY stupidly designed lockers...style over functionality at its least practical.   No pool, no jacuzzi, and after the steam room broke down several times in 2016...corporate has decided "no steam" either.   The only "luxury" is a small sauna that's a crowd with six people and not even hot. -  None of this describes the two Hollywood LA Fitness gyms, which DO have all the trimmings.  So, if all you want to do is work out and go home, with no sense of the "spa experience" whatsoever, then you'll be fine with the 5950 Wilshire location.  One nice touch is that the cardio machines look out across a pond (corporate concrete) to the front entrance of LACMA, where the action never seems to stop.   Compared to other LA Fitness gyms all over Los Angeles, my Two Star vote is being generous.<//Review>

< review>
Kobobgee Grill made my taste buds dance! I stuck with the Mezzas ‚Ä¶hummus, muhamarah, and warak inab (stuffed grape leaves).  I‚Äôm still salivating while writing this review. This is seriously great food. Most people think they‚Äôve eaten hummus. Grocery store hummus bears little resemblance to the real thing. Kabobgee‚Äôs hummus is smooth and rich and plate-lickable. Happily it and the muhamarah (really where has this been all my life!)  is served with minutes old pita. OMG the pita, fresh, hot, thin, with a crisp crust.  Back to the muhamarah, most people have never tasted this sweet, tart, rich, concoction of walnuts, mild red pepper, pomegranate and other mystery ingredients. Order it. And then place an order to take home so you don‚Äôt have to share. Speaking of not sharing, I had intended to share my warak inab with my friends. After one lemony, savory, yummy bite‚Äîno way. These are stuffed grape leaves like mama would have made if mama was Middle Eastern. Why are you still reading? Ge thee to Kobobogee!< /review>

Disappointing on many levels, probably the worst whole foods I've ever been to.  Consistently poor selection in the buffet section that almost never changes, the pizza section barely rivals Domino's. Missing a lot of goods present at other locations. Special orders never arrive, nobody calls especially in the meat and cheese dept. < text>
Today I discovered that the Salmon Chowder - does not have salmon in it.  The clerk was very helpful and called about my question after I read the ingredients.   The answer was that there is salmon in the fish broth that is used.

Secondly, the sandwich I ordered from the deli was over $8.00 - which I'm willing to pay for a great sandwich.  The bread tasted stale.

And the cole slaw I bought - I'm sure at a premium price - wasn't tasty at all.  We threw it away.

I'm wondering about other aspects of the business - is the organic raw almond butter - that is $17+ /lb - really organic - really raw?  I switched to Trader Joes for that months ago.

I also question whether the salmon served in the seafood deli that is bbqed and marinated - could it be a fish substitute.  When I recently served it, a guest asked if it were another fish.  Now I'm wondering about that.

I'm done with Whole Foods.  I've tried my best - despite the high prices - to appreciate freshness and organic food - what I associate with Whole Foods.  And, the staff are friendly, the store arranged in an interesting structure.  I'm very disappointed.< /text>

< review>
Today, I was in the Santa Barbara Whole Foods. Every Whole Foods I've regularly shopped is better: San Francisco, Monterey, Sausalito, etc. I asked a 'partner' in the tiny cosmetics/supplements department to double-check the micro-product number on a lip-liner to ensure I bought my favorite. I'd forgotten my glasses, and the colors of several represented micro-shade differences.

Her eyes blinked in stupefaction: "Me check? Are you lazy? Stupid? Recovering from a stroke? Do you not read English? Do I look like your slave girl?"

After her existential crisis had run its course, she begrudgingly checked the numbers and lined the two pencils side-by-side holding them up to me, like: "See 'El-Dumbo. Exactly the same."

I wanted the precise color as before as received countless compliments. I bought it with her assurance.

Made the long slog of a trek back and in front of a well-lit mirror applied the lip-liner. Hmm, looks different. Put my glasses on and the numbers/product weren't identical.

So now will need to walk all the way back tomorrow to exchange when this store regards returns as something akin to selling infants on the black market.

I realize there are actual problems in the world. I share some of them. But when you find your perfect shade and are willing to fork $18. over for it....is it really an unspeakable imposition to ask the department Whole Foods 'partner' absorbed in examining her cuticles to spend one focused minute to verify that you have the product you desire from the countless others that look identical until applied at home?

An added observation is that this store has the most disharmonious music/speakers of any Whole Foods, ever. When Whole Foods generally has toe-tapping, puts you in a stellar-mood songs playing. IF there is a Whole Foods in Calcasieu Parish, Louisiana..I promise the music and speakers are better...because it is impossible to be worse than in SB.< /review>

<review>Hello,

Yesterday I went to the wholefoods store in Santa Barbara. I put my phone, purse, and keys as I always do in my basket. I went shopping around, picking up a few items, including a BAC Foam Spray. A few minutes later I realize the foam spray is leaking all over the basket. It leaked into my iphone, which subsequently turned black and beeped constantly. I IMMEDIATELY went to costumer service, where a manager met with me. Danielle Iversen. She put my phone in a rice bag, and told me to contact the next day if I had any problems.

I called today. My phone is still broken. I was transferred to talk to Dave in management. Dave very rudely accused me of already having a broken phone, yes as Danielle saw my phone has a superficial crack on the back of it that had happened previously, no this did not result in it breaking the broken leaking bottle of BAC OUT did. He therefore told me it was my fault as I had a broken phone. Honestly, even if you do not want to claim any responsibility for the breaking of the phone from the liquid, for a man who does not know me to tell me about the state of my phone (he claimed there are chips in it and its missing pieces- which no its not he has not even seen it so to claim this to me rudely without any prior knowledge or info is absolutely terrible costumer service I come to wholefoods at least once a week with my family). I thought the way it was handled was super rude. I can understand that there might not be fault if you don't want to take responsibility for the broken BAC bottle, however to rudely throw it in my face when I was told to call back and discuss this yesterday, and tell me things about my phone which were not true was absolutely insulting. I would like to talk to someone about this as the situation was handled quite offensively, when I am the one now with a broken phone.
